any instrument or device which when used is likely to produce death or great
bodily harm. Any peace officer may wear or carry such weapons as may be
necessary and proper for the discharge of his official duties.



(Code 1972, § 22-48)



   State law reference—Carrying concealed weapons, SDCL § 22-14-1.



Sec. 11-87.  Drawing deadly weapons.



   No person, except officers of the law in the execution of their duties
or a person in self-defense, shall, in the city, draw a pistol, revolver,
knife or any other deadly or dangerous weapon so that the same may be used
against or upon another person.



(Code 1982, § 22-510)



Sec. 11-88.  Reckless discharge of firearm or shooting of bow and arrow;
trip device.



   Any person who recklessly discharges a firearm or recklessly shoots a
bow and arrow or sets a device designed to activate a weapon upon being
tripped or approached, and leaves it unmarked or unattended by a competent
person or has in his possession a loaded firearm while he is intoxicated is
guilty of a misdemeanor.



(Code 1982, § 22-500)



   State law reference—Similar provisions, SDCL § 22-14-7.



Sec. 11-89.  Hunting and discharge of firearms in rural service district.



   The owner of a parcel of real estate containing at least twenty (20)
contiguous acres located within a rural service district may hunt, control
predators, pests and feral animals on such property, or permit such activity
by others on such property, provided all such activities comply with South
Dakota law.  City ordinances governing such activities shall apply upon the
removal of any property from the rural service district. 



(Ord. No. 1039, 11-6-06)



Secs. 11-90—11-99. Reserved.



ARTICLE VI. MINORS



Sec. 11-100.  Definitions.



   For the purpose of this section the following terms, phrases, words,
and their derivations shall have the meanings given in this section.



   Minor is any person under the age of eighteen (18) who is not legally
emancipated.



   City is all area within one mile beyond the city limits of Spearfish.



   Custodian is any person over the age of eighteen (18) who is in loco
parentis to a juvenile.



   Guardian is any person other than a parent who has legal guardianship
of a juvenile.



   Juvenile is any person under the age of eighteen (18) who is not
legally emancipated.



   Parent is the natural or adoptive parent of a juvenile.



   Public place shall mean any street, alley, high-way, sidewalk, park,
playground, or place to which the general public has access and a right to
resort for business, entertainment, or other lawful purpose.



   In loco parentis is in the place of a parent, instead of a parent,
charged, factitiously, with a parent's rights, duties, responsibilities.



(Ord. No. 822, 4-21-97)



Sec. 11-101.  Purpose.



   The purpose of this section is to regulate the presence of juveniles on
the streets and other public places in the city during late-night hours. The
city has a compelling interest in said regulation due to the increase of
juvenile delinquency in the city. It is a compelling interest and goal of the
city to protect the public from the illegal acts of juveniles committed after
the curfew hours and also to protect the juveniles from improper influences
and from criminal activity that occurs after the curfew hour. It is also the
intent of this section to help parents control their children.



(Ord. No. 822, 4-21-97)



Sec. 11-102.  Curfew hours.



   It shall be unlawful for any juvenile to be or remain in or upon any
public place, either on foot or in a motor vehicle, after the hour of 12:00
midnight or before the hour of 5:00 a.m. on any day of the week, unless
accompanied by their parent, guardian, or custodian.



(Ord. No. 822, 4-21-97)



Sec. 11-103.  Exceptions to curfew.



   The provisions of this article imposing a curfew on minors shall not
apply to a juvenile accompanied by their parent, guardian, or custodian or
where the juvenile is upon an emergency errand or legitimate business, or
other reasonably necessary travel directed or authorized by their parent,
guardian, or custodian.



   Further, it shall not be a violation of this section for any juvenile
to attend a special function or entertainment sponsored by any church,
school, club or other organization if such juvenile can establish that such
attendance is with the specific permission of said juvenile's parent,
guardian, or custodian.



(Ord. No. 822, 4-21-97)



Sec. 11-104.  Responsibility of parents.



   It shall be unlawful for the parent, guardian, or custodian of a
juvenile to knowingly permit the violation of these sections. It shall not be
a violation of these sections if the exceptions to curfew are applicable.



(Ord. No. 822, 4-21-97)



Sec. 11-105.  Responsibility and procedures of officers.



   It shall be the right of any authorized officer or person to arrest or
detain any juvenile or person in violation of these sections, and make
reasonable attempts to notify the juvenile's parent, guardian, or custodian
regarding violations of these sections. A summons and complaint citation form
will be completed as per procedure, with a POA option, and handled as a
routine traffic violation in magistrate court.



(Ord. No. 822, 4-21-97)



Sec. 11-106.  Penalty.



   Violation of any provisions of these sections will be punished in
accordance to a Class 2 Misdemeanor. Enforcement of any provisions of these
sections will be in compliance of sections 17-51 to 17-64. Bond for
violations of any provisions of these sections will be per bond schedule or
as determined by the court.



(Ord. No. 822, 4-21-97)



Sec. 11-107.  Construction and severability.



   The city does not intend a result that is absurd, impossible to execute
or unreasonable. It is intended that the curfew ordinance codified in these
sections be held inapplicable in such cases, if any, where its application
would be unconstitutional. Constitutional construction is intended and shall
be given.



   The city does not intend to violate the Constitution of the State of
South Dakota or the Constitution of the United States of America.
Severability is intended throughout and within the provisions of the curfew
ordinance codified in these sections.



   If any provision including any exception, part, phrase or term, or the
application thereof to any person or circumstances is held to be invalid, the
application to other persons or circumstances shall not be affected thereby
and validity of the curfew ordinance codified in these sections in any or
other respects shall not be affected.



(Ord. No. 822, 4-21-97)



CHAPTER 12 MOBILE HOMES, MANUFACTURED HOMES AND PARKS*




   Art. I.    In General, §§ 12-1—12-2





   Art. II.    Manufactured Home Parks and Subdivisions, §§
12-3—12-12





      Div. 1.   Generally, §§ 12-3—12-5





      Div. 2.   Placement and Connection Permits, §§ 12-6—12-10





      Div. 3.   Maintenance of Park, §§ 12-11—12-12




   *Cross references—Consuming, blending, possessing, alcoholic
beverages in public places prohibited and the disposal of containers
containing alcoholic beverages restricted, § 4-17; buildings and building
regulations, Ch. 6; barbed wire and electrified fences prohibited, § 6-1;
building construction standards, § 6-26 et seq.; building permit fees, §
6-29; pole buildings prohibited in certain areas, § 6-32; numbering of
buildings, § 6-76 et seq.; fire protection and prevention, Ch. 7; burning of
trash, leaves and any other material or product prohibited, § 7-1; sale or
discharge of fireworks prohibited, § 7-3; fire prevention code adopted, §
7-46; storage of explosives, blasting agents, etc., restricted, § 7-49;
flood prevention and protection, Ch. 8; development permit required, § 8-31;
residential construction standards, § 8-77; flood prevention and protection
requirements for manufactured homes, §§ 8-79 and 8-80; health, sanitation
and nuisances, Ch. 9; peddlers' regulations, § 10-196 et seq.; abandoned
vehicles, § 17-501 et seq.; trees on private property, § 19-73 et seq.;
development standards for mobile home parks, Appendix A, Zoning Art. V.1.A;
sign regulations, Appendix A, Zoning Art. V.6.



ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL



Sec. 12-1.  Definitions.



   Manufactured home shall mean a moveable or portable unit, designed and
constructed to be towed on its own chassis (comprised of frame and wheels,
whether or not such wheels have been removed) and designed to be connected to
utilities for year-round occupancy. The term shall include:



   (1)   Units containing parts that may be folded, collapsed or
telescoped when being towed and that may be expanded to provide additional
cubic capacity.



   (2)   Units composed of two (2) or more separately towable
components designed to be joined into one (1) integral unit capable of being
separated again into the components for repeated towing.



The term ‘manufactured home’ shall include units designed or designated
to be used for residential, commercial, educational or industrial purposes,
excluding, however, recreational vehicles and other trailers and also
excluding manufactured homes, recreational vehicles, and other trailers
placed on the grounds of the Black Hills Airport pursuant to a ground lease.
For purposes of this Chapter and Appendix A to Ord. 1201, the terms
manufactured home and mobile home shall be interchangeable.



   Manufactured home park or subdivision shall mean any parcel (or
contiguous parcels) of land divided or arranged into two (2) or more
manufactured home lots for owner occupancy, rent or sale.



   Manufactured home space means a defined plot of ground or lot within a
manufactured home park which is designed for and designated as the location
for two (2) or more automobiles and one (1) manufactured home, and not used
for any other purposes whatsoever other than the customary accessory uses.



(Ord. 1201, 10-20-14; Ord. 1279, 5-7-18)



   Cross reference—Definitions and rules of construction generally, §
1-2.



Sec. 12-2.  Nonconforming use.



   Any manufactured home within the city limits and not in a manufactured
home park or campground is hereby declared a non- conforming use.



(Ord. 1201, 10-20-14)



ARTICLE II. MANUFACTURED HOME PARKS AND SUBDIVISIONS



DIVISION 1. GENERALLY



Sec. 12-3.  Manufactured home parks subdivision minimum standards.



   (a)   All manufactured home parks/subdivisions shall comply with the
requirements of Article V, Section 1 of Appendix A to Ord. 1201.



   (b)   The owner of a manufactured home park shall at all times
operate the park in compliance with the Revised Ordinances of the City of
Spearfish, and shall provide adequate supervision to maintain the park, its
facilities and equipment in good repair in a clean and sanitary condition at
all times.



(Ord. 1201, 10-20-14)



Sec. 12-4.  Manufactured home parks maintenance.



   The owner of a manufactured home park shall at all times operate the
park in compliance with the Revised Ordinances of the City of Spearfish, and
shall provide adequate supervision to maintain the park, its facilities and
equipment in good repair and in a clean and sanitary condition at all times.



(Ord. 1201, 10-20-14)



Sec. 12-5.  Owner’s right of entry to make repairs.



   It shall be the duty of every occupant of a manufactured home park to
give the owner thereof or his agent or employee access to any part of such
manufactured home park or its premises at reasonable times for the purposes
of making such repairs or alterations as are necessary to effect compliance
with this article, or with any lawful regulations adopted thereunder or with
any lawful order issued pursuant to the provisions of this article.



(Ord. 1201, 10-20-14)



DIVISION 2. PLACEMENT AND CONNECTION PERMIT*



Sec. 12-6.  Permit Required.



   It shall be unlawful for any person to set- up, place, establish, or
connect to utilities any manufactured home within the jurisdiction of the
city without first obtaining a Placement and Connection Permit issued by the
city building official. The permit fee shall be as established by resolution
as approved by the City Council.



(Ord. 1201, 10-20-14)



Sec. 12-7.  Placement of manufactured home.



   The placement of a manufactured home located on any lot within the
jurisdiction of the city shall meet the requirements of this chapter and must
be located according to the requirements of the Zoning Ordinance Appendix A,
Article V. Section 1.A Manufactured home parks/subdivisions. If the owner of
the manufactured home also owns the lot where the home is placed, the home
shall be placed on a foundation approved by the building official. 
Manufactured homes located within a manufactured home park or leased lot may
either be placed on a permanent foundation or on footing pads and piers as
approved by the building official.



(Ord. 1201, 10-20-14)



Sec. 12-8.  Conditions of support and anchoring.



   All manufactured homes shall be supported and anchored in accordance
with the manufacturers installation instructions, the Federal Model
Manufactured Home Installation Standards 24 CFR 3285, or as approved by the
city building official.



(Ord. 1201, 10-20-14)



Sec. 12-9.  Initial inspection.



   All blocking, piers, anchoring, plumbing, and mechanical work shall be
completed and inspected by the building official prior to the installation of
skirting. Only the area directly behind a landing or deck may be skirted
prior to the required inspection. Manufactured homes may not be occupied
until the initial inspection has been completed and approved.



(Ord. 1201, 10-20-14)



Sec. 12-10.  Final inspection.



   A final inspection of the manufactured home by the building official is
required upon the installation of skirting, porches, steps, landings and
guardrails. Approved residential numbering must be attached to the home prior
to final inspection.



   (1)   The location and width of roadways and walkways.



   (2)   The location of water and sewer lines, storm drains and catch
basins.



   (3)   The location and size of the recreation area.



(Code 1982, § 21-304; Ord. 1201, 10-20-14)



DIVISION 3. MAINTENANCE OF PARK



Sec. 12-11. Drainage.



   Every manufactured home park shall be located on a well-drained site,
and shall be so located that its drainage will not endanger any water supply.
Individual manufactured homes shall be placed to provide positive drainage
around the home.



(Ord. 1201, 10-20-14)



Sec. 12-12. Use of spaces generally.



   It shall be unlawful for any person operating a manufactured home park
to allow any manufactured home to be occupied unless the manufactured home is
situated on a manufactured home space.



(Ord. 1201, 10-20-14)



         



   *Cross-reference—Finance, § 2-161 et seq.



CHAPTER 13 SOLID WASTE*




   Art. I.   In General, §§ 13-1—13-25





   Art. II.   Collection, §§   13-26—13-41





   Art. III.   Restricted Use Site, §§ 13-42—13-50





   Art. IV.   Rates, Charges, Billing Procedure, §§ 13-51—13-54




   *Cross references—Administration, Ch. 2; animals, Ch. 5; buildings
and building regulations, Ch. 6; fire protection and prevention, Ch. 7;
burning of trash, leaves and any other material or product prohibited, §
7-1; fire prevention code adopted, § 7-46; flood prevention and protection,
Ch. 8; health, sanitation and nuisances, Ch. 9; license required for solid
waste collectors and haulers, § 10-251 et seq.; streets, sidewalks and other
public places, Ch. 14; streets and public rights-of-way, § 14-26 et seq.;
sidewalks, § 14-76 et seq.; subdivisions, Ch. 15; abandoned vehicles, §
17-501 et seq.; utilities, Ch. 18; vegetation, Ch. 19; zoning, App. A.



SOLID WASTE ADMINISTRATIVE RATES & POLICIES



The following policies and fees shall control excess garbage, loose garbage
placed in containers, pickup services, truck services, clean up containers,
and automobile disposal for City of Spearfish residential and commercial
customer accounts.



   1.   Residential Garbage -



      •   35-gallon container, available upon request in lieu of
the 65-gallon container, collected once a week.



      •   65-gallon container collected once per week.



      •   95-gallon container, available upon request in lieu of
the 65-gallon container, collected once per week.



      •   Residential customers who request an extra pickup of
their 35, 65, or 95 gallon container or who missed their regular garbage
pickup day and request their container be emptied, will be charged an extra
pickup fee equivalent to respective monthly pick up charges.



   2.   Loose Garbage in the containers will not be tolerated and
violators may be charged double the standard rate per occurrence per month.



   3.   Requested Special Pick up Service — The City will provide
pick up service for residential customers. Customers must contact the Public
Works Office to make a reservation. The following items are accepted:



      a.   Furniture, mattresses, & box springs



      b.   Appliances



         •   Appliances that do NOT use freon



         •   Containing freon — Appliances will be taken to
the Belle Fourche landfill and will NOT be accepted at the Rubble Site



   4.   Truck Services — The City may provide a truck for City
residents’ use based on availability. Spearfish residents with a
current/up-to-date account can reserve a truck through the Public Works
Office and authorize the payment to be added to their monthly utility bill.



   Trucks are delivered and removed by City staff during normal business
hours. The truck will be parked on paved or graveled surfaces only. The City
will not be responsible for rutting or driveway damage.



      •   Residents may not mix loads



      •   Residents may not operate the truck



   Allowed Items:



      •   Branches (by themselves)



      •   Shingles (no paper or plastic)



      •   Concrete, asphalt, dirt and rock (may be combined or
separate)



   Items not allowed:



      •   Plastic



      •   Cardboard



      •   Treated lumber



      •   Hazardous materials



      •   Household garbage



   5.   Clean up Containers – TThe City will provide a 300 or 450
gallon-automated container to residential and commercial customers with
current up-to-date accounts for the disposal of material associated with
general clean up.



      •   Material considered being hazardous, lumber, tires,
batteries, or metal may not be placed in the container.



      •   Container contents are disposed of at the Belle Fourche
Landfill.



      •   If the customer extends the use of the container beyond
thirty (30) days, there is an additional fee.



      •   Requests for containers must be made to the Public Works
Department and the fee will be added to the customer’s monthly billing.



      •   The customer is responsible for any loss or damaged
container, other than normal wear, and will be charged accordingly.



   6.   Trees, branches, and yard waste —



      a.   The City will NOT collect these items unless specifically
authorized by the City Council.



      b.   Residential customers may request truck service for trees
and branches. (Refer to residential truck service use and rate policy.)



      c.   Christmas tree disposal — The City will provide free of
charge, collection and disposal service to residential customers with
specific pick up times and dates determined by the Public Works Department.
Christmas trees may also be taken to Restricted Use Site during hours of
operation free of charge.



   7.   Tires —



      •   Only tires without rims will be accepted at the
Restricted Use Site.



      •   Tires with rims will NOT be accepted.



      •   The City will NOT provide pickup or truck service for
tire disposal.



   8.   Used oil & antifreeze will be accepted free of charge at the
Canyon Street Shop during business hours. Oil and antifreeze must be in
separate containers and labeled.



   9.   Rubbish, building material, and metal — These items are
described in the attached permit and will be accepted at the Spearfish
Restricted Use Site during posted operating hours. Fees will reflect current
disposal rates and are collected prior to disposal.



   10.   Batteries will be accepted free of charge at the Spearfish
Restricted Use Site. The site operator must check in batteries.



(Ord. No. 1103, 9-21-09; Ord. 1144, 9-19-11)



ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL



Sec. 13-1.  Definitions.



   The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter,
shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the
context clearly indicates a different meaning:



   Commercial shall be given its ordinary meaning. In addition, multi-unit
structures not having separately and individually metered domestic units for
water and/or sewer service shall be classified as commercial.



   Domestic shall mean an individual residential dwelling unit whose
primary use is for residential purposes, whether located in a single or
multi-unit structure that is separately and individually metered for water
and/or sewer service.



   Garbage shall mean kitchen refuse, cans, bottles, paper, cardboard,
plastics, and other waste materials ordinarily originating on household or
commercial premises. The word "garbage" shall not include flammable materials
as described in section 13-28, heavy accumulations as described in section
13-29, or certain wastes as described in section 13-30.



   Rubbish shall mean accumulations of clipped grass, tree leaves, tree
limbs and branches, and construction debris. The word "rubbish" shall not
include flammable materials as described in section 13-28, heavy
accumulations as described in section 13-29, or certain wastes as described
in section 13-30. Disposal of rubbish shall be at the expense of the party
responsible for the same.



(Code 1982, § 16-100; Ord. No. 851, 12-21-98; Ord. No. 941, 2-18-03)



   Cross reference—Definitions and rules of construction generally, §
1-2.



Sec. 13-2.  Littering prohibited generally.



   It shall be unlawful for any person to throw, drop, cast, or deposit
upon any street, alley, sidewalk or any yard or premises, public or private,
any filth of any kind, or cans, paper, trash, paper containers, bottles,
refuse, or any other form of litter or waste matter.



(Code 1982, § 16-110; Ord. No. 941, 2-18-03)



   Cross reference—Nuisances, § 9-26 et seq.



Secs. 13-3-13-25.    Reserved.



ARTICLE II. COLLECTION



Sec. 13-26.  Supervision.



   All garbage and rubbish accumulated in the city shall be collected,
conveyed and disposed of under the supervision of the common council.



(Code 1982, § 16-200; Ord. No. 631, § 16-200, 12-21-87; Ord. No. 941,
2-18-03)



Sec. 13-27.  Domestic garbage collection.



   The city shall be solely responsible for the collection and disposal of
all domestic garbage as defined in section 13-1. All domestic units within
the city shall pay the rates specified in section 13-53 et seq. and shall
comply with the following rules and regulations pertaining to the collection
of garbage:



   (1)   Domestic units of the city, subject to this article, shall
comply with automated collection approved by the city in the manner which
follows.



      a.   All domestic units as defined shall select a city issued
automated collection container as specified in section 13-53.



      b.   Domestic units may select multiple automated collection
containers as specified in section 13-53.



      c.   Only city issued automated collection containers shall be
allowed for use as garbage containers.



      d.   If the container is stored outside, it shall be kept so
as to protect the container and its contents from animals. Garbage placed in
the containers shall be bagged and tied to prevent blowing during collection.
Loose garbage placed in the container will not be allowed and violators may
be penalized as per section 13-32.



      e.   Domestic unit users shall place the automated collection
containers in a location suitable and readily accessible for collection by
the automated collection truck on the scheduled collection day. Containers
shall be removed from the curb within twenty-four (24) hours after emptied.
Containers shall not be stored at a location closer to the curb than the
front of the residence.



      f.   If the city has entered into a contract with a private
recycling company for domestic curbside recycling services, customer may
elect to request curbside recycling pickup from that private company for a
monthly fee. Customer must follow all established rules relating to pick-up
dates and times, pick-up locations, containers, and other specifications. No
person or entity may use city property or rights of way to deposit or pick-up
recycling other than the sole private recycling company under contract with
the city.



   (2)   Residents of the city are responsible for picking up garbage
from tipped containers.



   (3)   If an automated collection container issued by the city
becomes unusable because of damages resulting from the automated collection
truck, the city will replace the container at no cost to the domestic unit
resident. However, if an automated collection container becomes unusable due
to damages resulting from causes other than the automated collection truck,
the domestic unit resident shall be responsible to purchase a new container
from the city.



(Code 1982, § 16-210; Ord. No. 631, § 16-210, 12-21-87; Ord. No. 814, § 1,
12-2-96; Ord. No. 851, 12-21-98; Ord. No. 941, 2-18-03; Ord. No. 1193, 7-7-14)



Sec. 13-28.  Disposition of flammable materials.



   Highly flammable, explosive materials, and toxic materials will not be
placed in containers for regular collection or disposal but shall be disposed
of as directed by the city supervisor of sanitation at the expense of the
owner or possessor thereof.



(Code 1982, § 16-140; Ord. No. 941, 2-18-03)



   Cross reference—Fire prevention and protection, Ch. 7.



Sec. 13-29.  Disposition of heavy accumulations.



   Heavy accumulations such as earth or dirt, brick, broken concrete,
lumber ashes, plaster, sand or gravel, large dead trees, automobile frames or
parts, batteries, appliances, furniture, and other bulky, heavy materials,
shall be disposed of at the expense of the owner or person controlling the
same.



(Code 1982, § 16-150; Ord. No. 941, 2-18-03)



   Cross reference—Buildings and building regulations, Ch. 6.



Sec. 13-30.  Disposition of certain wastes.



   Wastes from lumber yards, building material suppliers, building
contractors, offal from meat and other packing plants, waste oil, batteries,
and used tires shall be disposed at the expense of the party responsible for
the same.



(Code 1982, § 16-160; Ord. No. 941, 2-18-03)



   Cross references—Construction standards, § 6-26 et seq.; licenses,
permits and business regulations, Ch. 10.



Sec. 13-31.  Frequency of collection and rates.



   Domestic unit services will provide one (1) pickup per week. Residents
which habitually exceed this volume of garbage will be contacted by the city
and special provisions made with respect to container and cost. Large
container charges will be as specified in section 13-53.



(Code 1982, § 6-210; Ord. No. 631, § 16-220, 12-21-87; Ord. No. 814, § 2,
12-2-96; Ord. No. 851, 12-21-98; Ord. No. 941, 2-18-03)



Sec. 13-32.  Extraordinary garbage collection policies.



   The public works administrator, subject to council approval, may adopt
policies and fees for excess garbage, loose garbage placed in containers,
collection by request of automobiles, appliances, trees, branches, and
rubbish of an extraordinary character. The public works administrator may
amend and modify the same with council approval. (Refer to solid waste
administrative rates and policies)



(Ord. No. 631, § 16-222, 12-21-87; Ord. No. 814, § 3, 12-2-96; Ord. No.
941, 2-18-03)



Sec. 13-33.  Commercial collection.



   Commercial operations within the city as defined in section 13-1 may
elect to be served by the city garbage service or by a private hauler. A home
occupation shall be considered to be a domestic unit as defined in section
13-1, but will be allowed to select commercial containers and shall pay the
commercial rates specified in section 13-51. The city shall be solely
responsible for collection of garbage from a home occupation. Commercial
operations shall be subject to the following rules and regulations:



   (1)   Replacement provisions for automated collection containers
shall be the same as for domestic units.



   (2)   Businesses may combine and request a large container to be
provided by the city to be charged according to section 13-53.



   (3)   All large containers must be situated on a hard surface,
located outside of public rights-of-way and be readily accessible to the
collection equipment.



(Ord. No. 631, § 16-230, 12-21-87; Ord. No. 814, § 4, 12-2-96; Ord. No.
851, 12-21-98; Ord. No. 941, 2-18-03)



Sec. 13-34 Private collection of business operations.



   Nothing in this article shall be construed to prohibit commercial
operations from hiring or employing nonmunicipal garbage collection and
removal.



(Ord. No. 631, § 16-231, 12-21-87; Ord. No. 851, 12-21-98; Ord. No. 941,
2-18-03)



Sec. 13-35.  Containers.



   (a)   City issued containers shall be constructed of polyethylene
with a molded hinged lid, which shall be kept closed. All containers will
have an identification number issued by the city.



   (b)   All private hauler containers provided to commercial units
shall be constructed of either metal or polyethylene and must have a suitable
watertight lid, which shall be kept closed.



(Code 1982, § 16-405; Ord. No. 941, 2-18-03)



Sec. 13-36.  Illegal use of containers.



   It shall be unlawful for any person to deposit garbage in a container
that is not issued to him or her by the city.



   Any person convicted of violating this section shall be fined not less
than twenty-five dollars ($25.00) and the current container fee.



(Ord. No. 686, 8-6-90; Ord. No. 851, 12-21-98; Ord. No. 941, 2-18-03)



Secs. 13-37—13-41.    Reserved.




ARTICLE III. RESTRICTED USE SITE*





   * Note—Title amended by Ord. No. 1043, passed 1-2-07.




Sec. 13-42.  Definition.



   The word "rubble" as used in this article shall mean trees, branches,
leaves, grass clippings, construction materials and lumber yard waste.



(Ord. No. 657, § 16-501, 6-19-89)



Sec. 13-43.  Authorized.



   The city is hereby authorized to operate and maintain a rubble site
facility in accordance with South Dakota Solid Waste Rules and Regulations,
SDCL Ch. 34A-6 and ARSD 74:27.



(Ord. No. 657, § 16-500, 6-19-89)



Sec. 13-44.  Days and hours of operation.



   The public works administrator shall establish the days and hours of
operation.



(Ord. No. 657, § 16-502, 6-19-89; Ord. No. 1116, 2-1-10)



Sec. 13-45.  Unlawful disposal.



   It shall be unlawful for any person to dispose of any hazardous, toxic
or household wastes at the rubble facility.



(Ord. No. 657, § 16-503, 6-19-89)



Sec. 13-46.  Fees.



   Fees for disposal at restricted use site to be set by resolution and
can be found in city schedule of fees.



(Ord. No. 657, § 16-505, 6-19-89; Ord. No. 873, 11-15-99; Ord. No. 941,
2-18-03; Ord. No. 1026, 5-15-06; Ord. No. 1102, 9-8-09)



Sec. 13-47.  Penalty for violation.



   The penalty for disposal of hazardous, toxic or any unauthorized wastes
at the restricted-use site shall be one hundred dollars ($100.00) per
violation.



(Ord. No. 657, § 16-504, 6-19-89; Ord. No. 1116, 2-1-10)



Sec. 13-48.  Free dumping.



   The city will allow dumping without charge from time to time for city
residents at the restricted-use site. The public works department will
administer implementation of this policy.



(Ord. No. 873, 11-15-99; Ord. No. 1116, 2-1-10)



Secs. 13-49—13-50.    Reserved.



ARTICLE IV. RATES, CHARGES, BILLING PROCEDURE*



   *Cross reference—Finance, § 2-161 et seq.



Sec. 13-51.  Special rates authorized.



   Wherever the collection of garbage, trash, and refuse from any premises
in the city shall exceed the normal amount for such premises so that the fee
prescribed for such collection is not fair and reasonable as applied to that
particular premises, the public works administrator, subject to council
approval, may establish policies and fees to accommodate special situations.



(Code 1982, § 16-300; Ord. No. 631, § 16-300, 12-21-87; Ord. No. 814, § 5,
12-2-96; Ord. No. 941, 2-18-03)



Sec. 13-52.  Reserved.



   Editor's note—Section 13-52 has been deleted and reserved by the
editor inasmuch as it appears to have been superseded by Ord. No. 941,
adopted Feb. 18, 2003. Said section 13-52 pertained to multiresidence rates
and derived from Ord. No. 631, § 16-221, adopted Dec. 21, 1987; Ord. No.
814, § 6, adopted Dec. 2, 1996; and Ord. No. 851, adopted Dec. 21, 1998.



Sec. 13-53.  Charges for collection by city.



   Rates, set by resolution, can be found in the city schedule of fees. 
Applicable sales tax shall also be charged for the collection and disposal of
garbage by the city.



(Code 1982, § 16-302; Ord. No. 631, § 16-310, 12-21-87; Ord. No. 650, § 1,
3-6-89; Ord. No. 691, 11-19-90; Ord. No. 714, 12-2-91; Ord. No. 737, 3-15-93;
Ord. No. 765, 11-21-94; Ord. No. 787, 12-18-95; Ord. No. 814, § 7, 12-2-96;
Ord. No. 941, 2-18-03; Ord. No. 1073, 10-15-07; Ord. No. 1088, 11-17-08; Ord.
No. 1103, 9-21-09)



Sec. 13-54.  Billing and collection procedure.



   (a)   The charge for collection and disposal of garbage shall be
payable by and chargeable to, either the owner or occupants of the property.
Such charge shall be noted on the monthly water billing and shall be payable
with and in addition to, such water bill. In the event of nonpayment of the
garbage collection and disposal charge, water service and garbage collection
may be forthwith discontinued by the city at such premises.



   (b)   In the event garbage collections shall be made by the city
under the provisions of this chapter from any premises not independently
served by the city water service and billed therefor, the owner or occupant
of the premises shall be billed for each month at the same time the water
users are billed. Such garbage collection charge shall be forthwith payable
to the city either by the owner or occupants of such premises. In the event
of failure of prompt payment of such charges, the city may discontinue
collection of garbage at such premises.



   (c)   In addition to the methods of billing and collecting the
charges for garbage gathering, the city finance officer, with the approval of
the common council, may from time to time adopt and use and may also enforce
as above provided, other methods of billing and collection as may be
reasonably efficient, feasible, and appropriate to the end that in every
case, all collection charges provided by this section shall be paid.



(Code 1982, § 16-301; Ord. No. 631, § 16-301, 12-21-87)



CHAPTER 14 STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND OTHER PUBLIC PLACES*




   Art. I.   In General, §§ 14-1—14-25





   Art. II.   Streets and Public Rights-Of-Way, §§ 14-26—14-75

§§ 14-131—14-155





   Art. VI.   Cemeteries, §§ 14-156—14-250





      Div. 1.   Generally, §§ 14-156—14-180
