ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL



Sec. 14-1.  Building permit.



   A building permit shall be required with the requisite fees associated
therewith prior to the construction of sidewalks and driveways required by
the city.



(Ord. No. 518, 11-10-82)



   Cross reference—Buildings and building regulations, Ch. 6.



Secs. 14-2—14-25.  Reserved.



ARTICLE II. STREETS AND PUBLIC RIGHTS-OF-WAY*



   *Cross references—Consuming, blending, possessing, alcoholic
beverages in public places prohibited and the disposal of containers
containing alcoholic beverages restricted, § 4-17; animals running at large
prohibited, § 5-1; burning of trash, leaves and any other material or
product prohibited, § 7-1; routes for vehicles transporting explosives, §
7-50; routes established for vehicles transporting houses and chemicals, §
7-51 et seq.; fire lanes established by the fire chief and chief of police,
§ 7-52; specific traffic regulations, § 17-186 et seq.; stopping, standing
and parking of vehicles, § 17-281 et seq.; truck routes established, §
17-406; abandoned vehicles, § 17-501 et seq.; street and park trees, §
19-71 et seq.; peddlers' regulations, § 10-196 et seq.; solid waste, Ch. 13;
street widths, grades, etc., in subdivisions, § 15-78 et seq.



   State law references—Streets and alleys, SDCL § 9-45-1 et seq.;
numbering of houses, SDCL § 9-45-2.



DIVISION 1. GENERALLY



Sec. 14-26.  Street grades.



   The grades of the streets and avenues in the city as theretofore
established and as shown on the street profiles on file in the office of the
public works administrator are hereby adopted as the official record of the
street grades in the city.



(Code 1982, § 18-110)



   State law reference—Authority to establish street grades, SDCL §§
9-45-1, 9-45-14.



Sec. 14-27.  Street name, prefixes; official map.



   (a)   The names of the streets lying easterly from Main Street shall
be designated as "East" and the names of the streets lying westerly of Main
Street shall be designated as "West." The prefixes shall be placed before the
proper names of the street as "East Colorado Street" or "West Colorado
Street."



   (b)   The names of the streets and avenues in the city are hereby
fixed and adopted in accordance with and as shown by the map of the city on
file in the office of the public works administrator, which map is hereby
designated and adopted as the official map of the city.



(Code 1982, §§ 12-305, 18-120)



   State law reference—Name of streets, avenues, SDCL § 9-45-2.



Sec. 14-28.  Obstruction of gutters.



   It shall be unlawful for any person to place, cause or maintain any
obstruction of whatsoever manner in any gutter or drainage ditch within the
city.



(Code 1982, § 18-130)



Sec. 14-29.  Removal, replacement of curbs and gutters.



   (a)   No person shall remove or cause to be removed any portion of
existing curb and gutter without first obtaining a written permit to do so
from the public works administrator. No such permit shall be issued for
removal of curb and gutter except in accordance with the provisions contained
herein.



   (b)   Application for such permit must be made in writing upon forms
furnished by the city. Such application shall contain the name and address of
the person making the application and the name and address of the contractor
or person who is to replace the curb and gutter.



   (c)   All such work shall be done under the jurisdiction of the
public works administrator and in accordance with the city Code and shall be
inspected upon completion by the constituted member of such department.



   (d)   All plans and specifications must conform to the following
minimum requirements before a permit for removal and replacement shall be
issued:



   (1)   The replacement of curb and gutter must conform to the
existing curb and gutter grade as established and designated by the official
grades of the streets of the city, and the profile on file in the office of
the public works administrator.



   (2)   If an existing expansion joint in the curb and gutter is
within five (5) feet of the end of the driveway opening, the existing curb
and gutter may be removed to the expansion joint, otherwise the existing curb
and gutter must be cut, making a neat edge truly at right angles to the edge
of the pavement and truly vertical.



   (3)   The new curb and gutter shall be constructed in a manner and
of a material equal at least to the existing curb and gutter adjacent thereto.



   (e)   It shall be the responsibility hereafter and required of the
property owner who removes or causes any other person to remove any portion
of curb and gutter to provide the costs for all materials, construction and
installation involved in replacing the curb and gutter, and all construction
and installation shall be performed according to plans and specifications of
the city.



   (f)   In the event any person fails to comply with the provisions of
this section, he shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and fined not less than
fifty dollars ($50.00).



(Code 1982, § 18-140)



Sec. 14-30.  Driveways.



   (a)   “Parkway” definition: the portion of the public
right-of-way which lies between the curb and gutter, and the adjacent
property line, or if no curb and gutter is present, it is the portion of the
public right-of-way which lies between the edge of the paved street and the
adjacent property line.



   (b)   It shall be the responsibility hereafter and required of all
property owners whose driveway connects to an existing paved street, paved
alley, or crosses over a public parkway to install a nonporous concrete or
bituminous driveway surface. The following are exceptions to this requirement:



      i.   In locations where the existing street or alleyway
providing access to the property is unpaved, the driveway shall be surfaced
with asphalt, concrete, gravel, asphalt millings, or similar loose material.



      ii.   For property zoned Rural Large Lot Single Family or
Agricultural, a paved surface is only required when the existing street
providing access to the property is paved, in which case the paving of the
driveway shall be required to extend only to the front setback and with a
minimum width of 12 feet. Beyond the front setback, gravel, asphalt millings,
or similar loose material is permitted.



   (c)   It shall be the responsibility hereafter and required of all
property owners whose driveway crosses over any portion of any public
sidewalk or public parkway to provide the costs for all materials,
construction and installation involved in surfacing the driveway with
nonporous concrete or bituminous material.



   (d)   Where a driveway of any kind of material is constructed across
the public sidewalk or public parkway, it shall conform to the sidewalk
grades as established and designated by the official grades of the sidewalks
of the city and the profiles on file in the office of the public works
administrator.



   (e)   All driveways shall be so graded between the gutter and the
sidewalk that it will not be necessary to change the established grade of
either and will not elevate or depress any portion of either. No part of such
driveway shall extend beyond the curbline in such manner as to change the
grade of such gutter or obstruct the free flow of water in such gutter. Where
elevations or depressions are necessary in the parkway strip adjoining the
curb and walks, the parkway shall be graded on both sides of the driveway to
a distance sufficient to create a gradual ascent or descent. Where driveways
cross open ditches in the parkways, adequate culverts shall be installed.



   (f)   In the event any person fails to comply with the provisions of
this section, he shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and fined not less than
fifty dollars ($50.00).



(Code 1982, § 18-150; Ord. No. 1165, 11-19-12; Ord. No. 1231, 1-19-16)



Sec. 14-31.  Surfacing of areas as behind lay-down curbs.



   (a)   It shall be the responsibility hereafter and required of the
property owner whose property adjoins or abuts lay-down curbing to install
within six (6) months a nonporous concrete or bituminous surface upon the
area behind the lay-down curbing which is used for parking, loading,
unloading or delivery purposes.



   (b)   It shall be the responsibility hereafter and required of such
property owner to provide the costs for all materials, construction and
installation involved in laying the nonporous concrete or bituminous surface.



   (c)   In the event any person fails to comply with the provisions of
this section, he shall be guilty of a misdemeanor.



(Code 1982, § 18-160)



Sec. 14-32.  Moving of buildings through streets, etc.



   (a)   It shall be unlawful for any person to move a building of any
kind over the streets or alleys of this city without first paying a fee of
fifty dollars ($50.00) and obtaining a permit to do so from the public works
department.



   (b)   When a permit shall be granted for the purpose of moving a
building over the streets of the city it shall be the duty of the public
works department to verify that the moving person or company has been
licensed by the city and submitted a certified check in the amount of one
thousand dollars ($1,000.00) to cover any damages to the city property which
might result from such use of the streets and alleys under the operation of
such permit.



   (c)   When the building has been moved as contemplated and allowed
by a permit under this section, it shall be the duty of the public works
administrator to carefully examine the route over which such building was
moved. If the person to whom such permit was granted repairs forthwith any
damages to the full satisfaction of the public works administrator, the
certified check collected as herein provided shall be refunded. Otherwise the
public works administrator shall cause such damages to be repaired and pay
for the same out of the certified check so collected and held by him, and
refund the remainder, if there be any, to the person from whom collected.



(Code 1982, §§ 18-400—18-402; Ord. No. 844, 6-1-98)



Sec. 14-33.  Location of street lights.



   (a)   Residential street lights, within the city, may be placed at
intersections. If there is a distance of over four hundred (400) feet between
intersections or on a dead-end street over four hundred (400) feet with a
cul-de-sac, the public works department shall determine the need and best
location for a light and make such recommendation to the public works
committee.



   (b)   The locations or spacing of street lights in commercial or
major thoroughfares shall be determined by the public works department. Such
location shall be based upon recommendation of the applicable electric
company as to candle power and coverage of light and shall be the most
efficient and economical to the city.



(Ord. No. 601, §§ 18-500, 18-501, 9-15-86)



Sec. 14-34.  Riding on toy vehicles prohibited.



   It shall be unlawful for any person traveling upon any coaster, sled,
roller skates or any toy vehicle to ride upon any street in the city.



(Code 1982, § 23-103)



Sec. 14-35.  Reserved.



   Editor's note—Ord. No. 817, adopted Feb. 18, 1997, repealed § 14-35,
which pertained to snow removal. See the Code Comparative Table.



Sec. 14-36.  Policy.



   It is hereby declared to be in the public interest to regulate and
restrict the parking and operation of vehicles on public streets during snow
removal efforts.



(Ord. No. 817, 2-18-97)



Sec. 14-37.  Snow storm information and advisory guide.



   The city administrator is hereby required to establish and maintain an
administrative policy entitled the City of Spearfish Snow Information and
Advisory Guide which describes how the city will address snow removal and
regulate such things as parking in snow conditions.  The policy has the
weight of law.



(Ord. No. 817, 2-18-97; Ord. No. 1112, 11-2-09)



Sec. 14-38.  Interference or obstruction of snow removal operations.



   It shall be unlawful for any person, or operator of any vehicle, to
interfere with or obstruct, or cause interference with or obstruction, of the
snow removal operations undertaken by the city and its employees. It shall
also be unlawful for any person to operate any vehicle in a manner not
reasonable or prudent, thereby creating a safety risk in relation to snow
removal operations.



(Ord. No. 817, 2-18-97)



Sec. 14-39.  Placement of snow.



   Residents and businesses shall not be allowed to place snow on public
boulevards and public streets. Exception: Property owners in the Downtown
Business Improvement District who have no ability to store snow on site will
be allowed to push snow onto the street if done before the city plows or
removes snow.  Any snow placed on the right-of-way along with snow already
on the street cannot exceed three (3) feet in height.



(Ord. No. 817, 2-18-97; Ord. No. 1112, 11-2-09)



Sec. 14-40.  Responsibility for snow removal on private driveways.



   The city will not plow snow from private property and will not open any
private driveways whether closed by city street plowing or other means.
Property owners will be responsible for snow removal of sidewalks in
compliance of section 14-80.



(Ord. No. 817, 2-18-97)



Sec. 14-41.  Additional power of administrative staff.



   The administrative staff shall have the power, during extreme snow
removal circumstances, to close any street or portion of street which is
under the jurisdiction of the city to all traffic and parking, if necessary,
for public safety and efficient removal of snow.



(Ord. No. 817, 2-18-97; Ord. No. 1112, 11-2-09)



Sec. 14-42.  Penalties.



   Violation of any provisions of this division, in addition to the
penalties contained herein, may be punished by a fine in accordance to a
Class 2 Misdemeanor. Illegally parked vehicles may be ticketed, towed and
impounded at owner's expense. Enforcement of any provisions of this division
will be in compliance of sections 17-51 to 17-64.



(Ord. No. 817, 2-18-97)



Secs. 14-43—14-50.    Reserved.



DIVISION 2. OBSTRUCTIONS AND ENCROACHMENTS



Sec. 14-51.  Definition.



   The word "encroachment," when used in this division, shall mean and
include any sign, awning, canopy, or marquee, billboard or other advertising
device, merchandise stand or display, building or other structure or other
use for private purposes of any character which exists in or rests upon or
projects above the right-of-way or any portion thereof of a public street.



(Code 1982, § 18-200)



   Cross reference—Definitions and rules of construction generally, §
1-2.



Sec. 14-52.  Restricted.



   It shall be unlawful, except as hereinafter provided, for any person to
erect, construct, install, place, maintain or allow to remain, or to permit
the erection, construction, installation, placing, maintenance or remaining
of any encroachment upon or above the right-of-way, or any portion thereof,
over street or other public way in the city.



(Code 1982, § 18-201)



Sec. 14-53.  Nonconforming encroachments.



   Any encroachment existing on the effective date of the ordinance from
which this division was derived, as heretofore permitted by the city, may be
continued for a period of ninety (90) days from and after such effective date
unless discontinued, or unless the same shall become defective and unsafe
prior to the expiration of such period, in which case the same shall be
removed by the owner or person permitting the erection, construction,
installation, placing or maintenance of the same; provided, however, that in
established business districts on such streets where the buildings are at the
property line and are continuous or very closely spaced, overhanging
encroachments are permitted under the following conditions:



   (1)   Awnings, canopies, marquees and similar installations
supported wholly from the face of the building shall be permitted, providing
that the edge of such encroachment be not less than three (3) feet back of
the face of the curb.



   (2)   Advertising or other similar signs supported wholly from the
front of the building shall be permitted to remain in place until such time
that they become functionally or structurally obsolete; such signs shall then
be removed.



   (3)   The replacements of encroachments, as allowed in (2) above,
will not be permitted.



(Code 1982, § 18-210)



Sec. 14-54.  Obstruction of traffic devices.



   In the event the encroachments referred to in section 14-53 by reason
of color or placement, obscure or in any way detract from the effectiveness
of highway signs or traffic signals, the city may cause the removal of such
encroachments in the manner hereinafter provided for the removal of any
encroachment in violation of this division.



(Code 1982, § 18-220)



Sec. 14-55.  Use of right-of-way.



   The use of the right-of-way by owners or lessees of abutting property
for the storage of vehicles, placement of portable signs or other private
use, is hereby prohibited on public streets or alleys.



(Code 1982, § 18-230)



Sec. 14-56.  Display of goods prohibited.



   The use of sidewalks or other areas of the right-of-way for the storage
or display of merchandise is prohibited on public streets.



(Code 1982, § 18-240)



Sec. 14-57.  Removal.



   Whenever any encroachment exists in violation of the provisions of this
division, the common council shall direct the city finance officer to
forthwith issue notice requiring the removal of such encroachment within a
time specified in such notice. If the owner of such encroachment, or his
agent, is known, such notice shall be a written notice served in person or by
mail upon such owner or agent. If the owner or agent is unknown, such notice
shall be published once in the official city paper. If the owner or his agent
shall fail or refuse to remove the encroachment within the time fixed in the
notice, the city shall cause the encroachment to be removed.



(Code 1982, § 18-250)



Sec. 14-58.  Reserved.



   Editor's note—Ord. No. 921, adopted Apr. 1, 2002, repealed § 14-58,
which pertained to permit for sign, marquee. See the Code Comparative Table.



Sec. 14-59.  Reserved.



   Editor's note—Ord. No. 921, adopted Apr. 1, 2002, repealed § 14-59,
which pertained to specifications for permitted signs, marquees. See the Code
Comparative Table.



Sec. 14-60.  Permission for artwork.



   Any person desiring to place sculpture, statuary, fountains, or other
artwork of any kind on or over public property shall first obtain permission
from the common council, which shall approve the artwork and location
thereof. Such artwork may not constitute a safety or traffic hazard.



(Ord. No. 901, 9-17-01)



   Editor's note—Ord. No. 901, adopted Sept. 17, 2001, amended the Code
by adding provisions designated as § 14-59. Inasmuch as there already exists
provisions so designated, the provisions of Ord. No. 901 have been included
herein as § 14-60 at the discretion of the editor. See the Code Comparative
Table.



Sec. 14-61.  Certain church signs permitted.



   Notwithstanding any ordinance or zoning regulation to the contrary,
each church located within the city shall be allowed to use the public
right-of-way to place two (2) directional and informational signs not
exceeding seven hundred twenty (720) square inches per sign on each side.
Both sides of a sign may be used if the sign is hung by a bracket. No fee or
permit is required for such sign.



(Ord. No. 958, 6-16-03)



Secs. 14-62—14-75.    Reserved.



ARTICLE III. SIDEWALKS*



   *Cross references—Consuming, blending, possessing, alcoholic
beverages in public places prohibited and the disposal of containers
containing alcoholic beverages restricted, § 4-17; animals running at large
prohibited, § 5-1; peddlers' regulations, § 10-196 et seq.; solid waste,
Ch. 13; sidewalk requirements in subdivisions, § 15A-88.



   State law reference—Sidewalks, SDCL § 9-46-1 et seq.



Sec. 14-76.  Installation required.



   (a)   Unless exempt under Chapter 15 [15A] or Appendix A, it shall
be the responsibility hereafter and required of all property owners of vacant
lots, that sidewalks be installed whenever a new building or dwelling be
constructed upon such vacant lots.



   (b)   Such sidewalks shall be completed at or before the time the
new building or dwelling is completed and shall be constructed and installed
according to city plans and specifications on file in the office of the
public works administrator.



(Code 1982, § 12-500; Ord. No. 922, 4-1-02)



Sec. 14-77.  Location of sidewalks.



   (a)   Sidewalks constructed in the city shall be located in
conformity with existing sidewalk locations, except the replacement of
sidewalks abutting the curb, whenever possible, shall conform to the
standards of this section.



   (b)   In the event no existing sidewalk location and in the case of
new subdivisions, sidewalk location shall be as follows:



   (1)   Five (5) feet from and parallel to the back of the curb.



   (2)   If no curb exists, parallel to and adjacent to the lot line.



The common council may permit exceptions where special conditions warrant.



(Code 1982, § 12-501; Ord. No. 697, 3-4-91)



Sec. 14-78.  Specifications.



   All sidewalks within this city shall be constructed and maintained in
compliance with specifications therefor promulgated in the city.



(Code 1982, § 12-502)



Sec. 14-79.  Discharge of rainwater.



   It shall be unlawful for any person to permit the rainwater from any
building discharge on and over the sidewalks.



(Code 1982, § 12-510)



Sec. 14-80.  Reserved.



   Editor's note—Ord. No. 951, adopted Apr. 21, 2003, repealed § 14-80,
which pertained to the duty to keep sidewalks clear of snow, and derived from
Code 1982, § 12-520; and Ord. No. 589, § 520, adopted Feb. 3, 1986. For
similar provisions see subsection 9-27(4).



Sec. 14-81.  Sidewalk snow and ice control.



   Property owners are responsible for controlling snow and ice buildup on
sidewalks.



(Code 1982, § 12-521)  (Ord. No. 1112, 11-2-09)



Sec. 14-82.  Building permits required prior to building of sidewalks and
driveways.



   (a)   A building permit shall be required with the requisite fees
associated therewith prior to the construction of sidewalks and driveways
required by the city.



   (b)   Section 301(b)(7) of the Uniform Building Code adopted in
section 6-26 adopted by the city is repealed and all other provisions of such
Code inconsistent with this section are likewise repealed.



   (c)   Unless changed by ordinance of the city, the provision
exempting sidewalks and driveways in any future edition of the Uniform
Building Code which may hereafter be adopted by the city, will likewise be
repealed and ineffective.



(Code 1982, § 12-532)



Sec. 14-83.  Restricted.



   It shall be unlawful for any person to erect, construct, install,
place, or to permit the erection, construction, installation, placing of any
encroachment upon or above any portion of any residential sidewalk in the
city.



(Ord. No. 703, 6-3-91)



Sec. 14-84.  Removal.



   Whenever any encroachment exists in violation of these provisions,
written notice shall be given the owner of record requiring removal within
fourteen (14) days. If the owner of record fails to remove the encroachment
within the time specified in the notice, the city shall remove the
encroachment at the owner's expense.



(Ord. No. 703, 6-3-91)



Sec. 14-85.   Public sidewalk maintenance.



   The maintenance of sidewalks located in city right-of-way including,
but not limited to, the area between the property line and street curb shall
be the responsibility of the owner, manager or lessee of the abutting
property.



   Such persons are jointly and severally liable for the maintenance and
replacement when required by the City of Spearfish according to the criteria
pertaining to sidewalk replacement.



(Ord. No. 1165, 11-19-12)



Secs. 14-86—14-100.     Reserved.



ARTICLE IV. ASSEMBLIES, PARADES, PROCESSIONS*



   *Cross reference—Consuming, blending, possessing, alcoholic beverages
in public places prohibited and the disposal of containers containing
alcoholic beverages restricted, § 4-17.



Sec. 14-101.  Permit required.



   It shall be unlawful for any person to organize or hold or participate
in any parade, meeting, assembly, outdoor concert or procession of persons
and/or vehicles on the streets, sidewalks or public parks of this city unless
such activity shall have first been authorized by a written permit issued by
the chief of police therefor.



(Code 1982, § 7-100; Ord. No. 746, 10-4-93; Ord. No. 835, 11-17-97)



Sec. 14-102.  Application for permit.



   The application for a permit required by this article shall contain the
following:



   (1)   The name and address of the applicant.



   (2)   The name and address of the person the applicant represents.



   (3)   The exact time and date of commencement and termination of
each act or activity desired.



   (4)   The purpose, location and route of such act or activity, if
applicable.



   (5)   The person, group, association or body to be authorized under
the permit to do such act or activity and the number of persons to
participate.



   (6)   The age of any minors who may participate in such activity,
and the name of the person who will be responsible for such minors.



   (7)   Such other relevant information as the chief of police may
require for the investigation of the applicant.



(Code 1982, § 7-101)



Sec. 14-103.  Contents of permit.



   Upon issuance of a permit required by this article, the same shall
contain therein all information contained in the application therefor and be
signed by the chief of police and a signed copy of the same shall be kept
with the application, both on file in the office of the chief of police.



(Code 1982, § 7-102)



Sec. 14-104.  Matters considered in determining issuance of permit.



   In deciding whether to issue a permit under the provisions of this
article, the chief of police shall consider:



   (1)   Number of persons to participate.



   (2)   Anticipated traffic conditions at the time and date proposed
for the activity.



   (3)   Schedule of other similar activities for which permits may
have been issued.



   (4)   Adequacy of adult supervision for any minors scheduled to
participate.



   (5)   Availability of city personnel whose presence on duty may be
required by the activity and by the necessity to protect the general public.



   (6)   Adequacy of public facilities in the location proposed for the
activity to accommodate the proposed activity and the normal public use of
public facilities in the proposed location.



(Code 1982, § 7-103)



Sec. 14-105.  Issuance.



   The permit required by the provisions of this article shall be issued
by the chief of police upon application therefor; provided, however, that
such permit may be denied or refused if it shall appear that the applicant
therefor or the act or activity requested by such application shall violate
any applicable provision of the Code, state law or city ordinance.



(Code 1982, § 7-104)



Sec. 14-106.  Time lapse between application, activity.



   It shall be unlawful for any activity authorized under this article to
commence within five (5) days from the date of the application therefor.



(Code 1982, § 7-105)



Sec. 14-107.  Deviation from permit.



   It shall be unlawful for any person participating in any act or
activity for which a permit has been granted under the provisions of this
article to deviate from or alter any of the terms or contents of such permit.



(Code 1982, § 7-106)



Sec. 14-108.  Display of permit.



   Every person having a permit issued under the provisions of this
article shall have such permit in his possession during the activity
permitted thereby, and shall display such permit upon the request of any law
enforcement officer. Failure to display such permit shall be deemed a
misdemeanor.



(Code 1982, § 7-107)



Sec. 14-109.  Revocation of permit.



   Any permit issued under the provisions of this article may be revoked
by the chief of police for the violation by the permittee of any applicable
provision of this Code, state law or city ordinance.



(Code 1982, § 7-108)



Sec. 14-110.  Dispersal of activity.



   Whenever the free passage of any street or sidewalk in the city shall
be obstructed by a crowd, congregation, parade, meeting, assembly or
procession, or the conduct of two (2) or more persons, except as authorized
by any permit issued pursuant to this article, the persons comprising such
group shall disperse or move when directed to do so by a police officer. It
shall be unlawful for any person to refuse and such refusal shall be a
violation of this article.



(Code 1982, § 7-109)



Sec. 14-111.  Enforcement.



   Nothing contained in this article shall prohibit the authority of any
officer to arrest a person engaged in any act or activity granted a permit
under this article, if the conduct of such person violates the laws of the
state, provisions of this Code or ordinances of this city, or unreasonably
obstructs the public streets and sidewalks of this city, or engages in acts
that cause, or would tend to cause, a breach of the peace.



(Code 1982, § 7-110)



Sec. 14-112.  Outdoor concerts regulated.



   (a)   Any outdoor concert consisting of live or recorded music held
in a public park or other public area shall end by 9:30 p.m. and shall be
conducted in such a manner as to not disturb the peace of the city.



   (b)   This section shall not apply to community designated events.



(Ord. No. 746, 10-4-93; Ord. No. 1134, 4-4-11)



Secs. 14-113—14-130.  Reserved.



ARTICLE V. USE OF MUNICIPAL RIGHTS-OF-WAY (ROW)
AND OTHER PROPERTIES*



   *Cross reference—Utilities, Ch. 18.



Sec. 14-131.  Supervision.



   The city engineer, or his or her designee, shall supervise all
excavations made for any purpose in the streets, alleys or public ground, and
shall require compliance with all the requirements of this article.



(Code 1982, § 18-300; Ord. 1221, 12-21-15)



Sec. 14-132.  Permit required.



   (a)   No person shall make or cause to be made any excavation in or
under any street, parking, sidewalk, alley or public ground without first
having obtained a ROW permit and a contractor’s license from the building
and development department. The permit will not be required to start
emergency work as may be necessary to protect existing structures. However,
the permit shall be obtained the morning of the first working day after such
work has commenced.



   (b)   Any person, other than a person holding a special event
permit, desiring to block, partially occupy, or interrupt the traffic flow of
any ROW for 30 minutes or more for any reason, shall be required to have a
ROW permit.



   (c)   The construction of driveways and sidewalks within the city's
corporate limits pursuant to a City of Spearfish building permit will include
a ROW permit at no extra charge.



   (d)   Any person starting any work in a municipal ROW without a ROW
permit shall be subject to fines set forth in section 1-14.



(Code 1982, § 18-310; Ord. No. 880, 4-17-00; Ord. 1221, 12-21-15)



Sec. 14-133.  Application for permit.



   (a)   Any person requesting a ROW permit shall make application to
the city engineer, or his or her designee.



   (b)   At a minimum, the application shall include the exact location
of the excavation, a detailed description of the work to be performed, the
purpose for the excavation, an illustration of the areas to be disturbed or
removed, and a timeline for the replacement of all materials. The city
engineer may approve temporary repairs in the event of inclement weather.



   (c)   Additional submittal documents, such as traffic control plans
and utility plans or profiles, may be required as determined by the city
engineer, based on the size or complexity of the project or other factors.



   (d)   Only licensed contractors may perform curb or street repairs.



(Code 1982, § 18-311; Ord. 1221, 12-21-15)



Sec. 14-134.  Permit fee.



   The fee for a ROW permit shall be the minimum base charge set by
resolution, per excavation, up to and including 400 feet. Beyond 400 feet,
the permit fee will be charged by the foot, commensurate with the base charge
listed above. A service repair permit shall be obtained in lieu of a ROW
permit for repair of water or sewer service lines. The permit fee for the
repair of city water and sewer service lines shall be waived.



(Code 1982, § 18-312; Ord. 1221, 12-21-15)



Sec. 14-135.  Condition of issuance.



   (a)   Every application for a ROW permit that involves excavation in
or under any street, parking area, or sidewalk shall be accompanied by:



      (1)   A certificate of insurance showing that the applicant
has in effect a statutory workmen's compensation insurance policy in the
amount of limits applicable for the State of South Dakota;



      (2)   A certificate of insurance showing that the applicant
has occurrence-based commercial general liability insurance or equivalent
form, with a limit of not less than $1,000,000 for each occurrence. If such
insurance contains a general aggregate limit, it shall apply separately to
this ROW permit or be no less than two times the occurrence limit. Such
insurance shall add the City of Spearfish and its employees as additional
insureds. Such certificate shall contain a statement to the effect that the
policy cannot be canceled or substantially altered without ten (10) days
prior written notice to the city; and



      (3)   A certificate of insurance showing that the applicant
has automobile liability insurance, with a limit of not less than $1,000,000
each accident. Such insurance shall include coverage for owned, hired, and
non-owned vehicles. Such certificate shall contain a statement to the effect
that the policy cannot be canceled or substantially altered without ten (10)
days prior written notice to the city.



   (b)   Each ROW permit issued shall contain a statement and shall be
issued only upon the express condition that the permittee shall refill the
excavation in accordance with the instructions of the city engineer, and
restore the pavement or surfacing, as the case may be, to its former
condition, and maintain it in such condition for a period of three (3) years
from the time of completion of the work authorized by the ROW permit.



(Code 1982, § 18-313; Ord. No. 780, 8-21-95; Ord. No. 880, 4-17-00; Ord.
1221, 12-21-15)



Sec. 14-136.  Refilling excavations.



   The city engineer shall adopt, amend and enforce a code of rules and
regulations which shall set forth the manner in which various types of
excavations shall be replaced.



(Code 1982, § 18-314; Ord. 1221, 12-21-15)



Sec. 14-137.  Restoring pavements or street surfacing to meet city
specifications.



   It shall be the duty of the city engineer to keep on file a copy of all
ROW permits, and to conduct periodic inspections of pavements or other street
surfacing disturbed pursuant to such permits. If a pavement or surface is not
restored to current city specifications, notice thereof shall be sent to the
permittee. The permittee shall return the pavement or surface to an approved
condition within a time period as specified by the city engineer. If the
permittee fails to restore and maintain such pavement or the surfacing
thereof, the city engineer shall arrange for the completion of the necessary
repairs. The original permittee shall pay a penalty to the city equal to one
and one-half (1.5) times the cost of the repairs. No other permit shall be
issued to an individual, or any person in his or her behalf, until
satisfaction of the penalty provided by this section has occurred. The city
engineer shall be consulted for typical street patching requirements.



(Code 1982, § 18-315; Ord. No. 1044, 1-2-07; Ord. 1221, 12-21-15)



Sec. 14-138.  Protection of public and surrounding properties.



   (a)   Any person receiving a permit to make excavations in or upon
any street, alley, sidewalk or public ground shall, during the progress and
continuance of the work, erect and maintain around the project area, both by
day and night, suitable guards, fences, lanterns and signals so as to prevent
injury to persons, animals orvehicles on account of such excavations. Such
lanterns shall be kept lighted from sundown until sunrise. Traffic control
will be determined by the city engineer, based on the specific project and
its proximity to roadways. If a traffic control plan is required, the
contractor will be required to use South Dakota Department of Transportation
(SDDOT) standard traffic control plates, which will be filed with the ROW
permit application. Larger projects may require traffic control plans
implemented by a SDDOT-approved contractor.



   (b)   It shall be unlawful for any person, owner, or occupant of any
lot to make or cause to be made any excavation adjacent to any street, alley,
public ground, sidewalk, or traveled road or roadway, unless appropriate
measures are implemented to prevent the injury of any person or animal.



   (c)   Any person making an excavation shall use all appropriate
control measure to prevent pollutants from entering neighboring properties
and waters of the state, including municipal storm drain conveyances and
natural drainage ways



(Code 1982, § 18-316; Ord. 1221, 12-21-15)



Sec. 14-139.  Reserved.



   Editor's note—Ord. No. 1221, adopted Dec. 21, 2015, repealed §
14-139, which pertained to the duty to safely guard excavations near
rights-of-way and derived from Code 1982, § 18-317. For similar provision
see subsection 14-138(b).



Sec. 14-140.  Ditch compaction.



   The city will not allow water soaking for compaction of trenches
resulting from utility placement or repairs. All trenches will be
mechanically tamped and compacted to a compaction factor of ninety-five
percent (95%) or greater. Testing of the trench compaction may be required,
at the discretion of the city engineer. Any person violating this article
shall be subject to fines set forth in section 1-14.



(Ord. No. 602, 9-15-86; Ord. No. 1044, 1-2-07; Ord. 1221, 12-21-15)



Secs. 14-141—14-155.    Reserved.



ARTICLE VI. CEMETERIES*



   *Cross references—Consuming, blending, possessing, alcoholic
beverages in public places prohibited and the disposal of containers
containing alcoholic beverages restricted, § 4-17; animals running at large
prohibited, § 5-1.



   State law references—Cemeteries generally, SDCL Ch. 34-27; authority
of city relative to cemeteries, SDCL § 9-32-13.



DIVISION 1. GENERALLY



Sec. 14-156.  Scope of article.



   The cemetery owned and operated by the city and known as Rose Hill
Cemetery shall be governed, managed, and operated under the provisions of
this article. A cemetery advisory board may be appointed by the mayor to give
input to the city on procedures and policies of the cemetery.



(Code 1982, § 6-200; Ord. No. 599, § 6-200, 9-15-86; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Sec. 14-157.  Employment of parks, recreation and forestry technician.



   The common council shall employ a parks, recreation and forestry
technician and such other help as may be necessary to properly tend and care
for the cemetery.



(Code 1982, § 6-210; Ord. No. 599, § 6-210, 9-15-86; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Sec. 14-158.  Parks, recreation, and forestry technician's duties generally.



   It shall be the duty of the parks, recreation, and forestry technician
to oversee the digging of graves; to properly care for and irrigate all
trees, shrubbery, flowers, and grass growing in the cemetery; to keep the
driveways, walks, and fences in good condition; to see that all markers and
monuments are not defaced or destroyed; to protect the property of the
cemetery; and to see that the provisions of this article, rules and
regulations of the council governing the cemetery are complied with in every
way.



(Code 1982, § 6-211; Ord. No. 599, § 6-211, 9-15-86; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Sec. 14-159.  Records generally.



   The public works office shall keep all records of the cemetery and
shall procure suitable books, blank forms, or other records, written and
electronic for the purpose. A map of the cemetery shall be kept in the public
works office and at the cemetery. The public works administrator shall
designate a public works employee to sell all lots and sign the permit for
disposition of dead human remains.



(Code 1982, § 6-212; Ord. No. 599, § 6-212, 9-15-86; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Sec. 14-160.  Rules, regulations.



   The administration and operation of the cemetery shall be under the
public works administrator, who may make such rules and regulations, which
shall be subject to the approval of the common council and kept on file in
the public works office.



(Code 1982, § 6-233; Ord. No. 599, § 6-213, 9-1586; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Sec. 14-161.  Handling of funds.



   All money received for the sale of cemetery lots, digging of graves,
special care, and other services about the cemetery shall be paid directly to
the city who shall give the proper receipts therefore, and shall be placed in
the general fund, which funds shall be used for the payment of the purchase
price of grounds, maintenance and improvements of the cemetery.



(Code 1982, § 6-242; Ord. No. 599, § 6-220, 9-1586; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Sec. 14-162.  Special conditions for blocks F and G of the cemetery.



   The following rules will be followed:



   (1)   All markers in these designated areas of the cemetery shall be
placed on the west side of the space facing east. Footstones shall be flush
with the surface of the ground.



   (2)   Concrete borders will not be allowed. Corner markers, if
desired, may be placed at the property owner's expense, and shall be flush
with the ground and no larger than four (4) square inches in surface area.



   (3)   No planting of any living trees, shrubs, flowers or plants is
allowed upon grave units, lots or in alleyways.



   (4)   Fences or hedges around or on grave units or around lots are
prohibited.



(Code 1982, § 6-235; Ord. No. 599, § 6-235, 9-1586; Ord. No. 799, 4-15-96;
Ord. No. 860, 4-19-99; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Sec. 14-163.  Plantings of trees, shrubs, flowers or plants.



   The planting of trees, shrubs, flowers or plants shall be prohibited at
the cemetery including gravespaces and the Rose Garden. As existing plantings
located on graves or in alleyways die, they shall not be replaced. Trees may
be planted as authorized by the parks, recreation, and forestry technician.



(Code 1982, § 6-236; Ord. No. 599, § 6-236, 9-1586; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Sec. 14-164.  Permanent headstone.



   A permanent headstone/marker should be placed within two (2) years of
burial.



(Ord. No. 799, 4-15-96; Ord. No. 1295, 11-19-18)



Sec. 14-165.  Concrete borders.



   Concrete borders around graves will not be allowed. Corner markers, if
desired, may be placed at the property owner's expense, and shall be flush
with the ground and no larger than four (4) square inches in surface area.
Any concrete border repair, when impracticable to be flush with the ground,
is grandfathered. If the curbing becomes unsightly, the family will be
responsible to repair the curbing. A reasonable attempt shall be made to
contact the family to repair the curbing. If there is no response from the
family or they are unable to be contacted, the city may remove the curbing
and replace the area with grass.



(Ord. No. 860, 4-19-99; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Sec. 14-166.  Permanent vases.



   Permanent vases shall only be placed within the grave space on the
sides of the concrete monument bases.



(Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Sec. 14-167.  Removal of grave markers prior to burial.



   A grave marker may be removed before grave digging and then the marker
replaced once the grave has been prepared. The cost for marker removal and
replacement will be at the owner's expense.



(Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02; Ord. No. 1295, 11-19-18)



Sec. 14-168.  Grave markers.



   One (1) upright marker shall be allowed per space. Additional markers
and footstones shall be placed flush with the ground.  The location of
markers on all graves shall be determined and at the discretion of the
cemetery staff.



(Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02; Ord. No. 988, 7-23-04)



Sec. 14-169.  Monument permit.



   A permit shall be required before placement, repair, engraving, etc. of
monuments. The permit shall be obtained through the cemetery office when the
following information has been furnished:



   (1)   Name of deceased.



   (2)   Block, section, lot and space ID of which monument placement
or work is to be done.



   (3)   Name of the monument company doing the placement or work.



   (4)   Type of work to be done and date placement or work is to be
completed.



   (5)   A diagram of the grave space(s) showing exact placement of the
monument(s).



(Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02; Ord. No. 1295, 11-19-18)



Secs. 14-170—14-180.  Reserved.



DIVISION 2. LOTS



Sec. 14-181.  Fees.



   All cemetery fees are set by Resolution and on file with the City
Finance Office.



(Code 1982, § 6-231; Ord. No. 595, 5-5-86; Ord. No. 599, § 6-240, 9-15-86;
Ord. No. 700, 4-15-91; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02; Ord. No. 1295, 11-19-18)



Sec. 14-182.  Settlement of sales transaction.



   All cemetery lots or graves spaces shall be settled for at the time of
purchase. No burials shall be made upon a lot for which the city has not
received settlement. Upon receipt of full payment, a perpetual care
certificate will be issued. Should there be an interment on a cemetery space
for which full payment has not been made, the city reserves the right to
disinter the remains and remove the burial, together with any monument or
other structure thereon, to some other portion of the cemetery equal in price
to the amount paid on such space, after the actual cost of removal has been
deducted.



(Code 1982, § 6-240; Ord. No. 599, § 6-241, 9-1586)



Sec. 14-183.  Resale of lots restricted.



   All cemetery lots or grave spaces shall be used for burial purposes
only and shall not be resold without the consent of the designated city
employee(s).



(Code 1982, § 6-241; Ord. No. 599, § 6-242, 9-1586; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Sec. 14-184.  Purchase of spaces at the Rose Garden.



   Spaces at the Rose Garden for burial and spreading of ashes shall be
purchased only in designated areas. Those areas shall be determined by the
designated city employee(s).



(Code 1982, § 6-250; Ord. No. 599, § 6-250, 9-15-86; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Sec. 14-185.  Care of ashes.



   When the ashes of a cremated body are to be interred in the cemetery or
Rose Garden, the ashes must be in a durable urn or in a strong metal or
concrete case. When burying in the Rose Garden, the container shall be no
larger than one (1) foot by one (1) foot.



(Code 1982, § 6-251; Ord. No. 599, § 6-251, 9-15-86; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Sec. 14-186.  Nameplates in Rose Garden.



   All five-inch by eight-inch nameplates at the Rose Garden shall have
the deceased's name, date of birth and date of death printed on them. The
five-inch by eight-inch plates shall be purchased through the cemetery office.



(Code 1982, § 6-252; Ord. No. 599, § 6-252, 9-15-86; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02;
Ord. No. 1295, 11-19-18)



Sec. 14-187.  Reserved.



   Editor's note—Ord. No. 1038, adopted Oct. 2, 2006, repealed §
14-187, which pertained to fees for burial in Rose Garden. See the Code
Comparative Table.



Sec. 14-188.  Items placed on graves.



   (a)   Wreaths and artificial flowers may be allowed on graves from
October 1 through April 1. Items will be allowed on graves three (3) days
prior to the observed Memorial Day holiday and ten (10) days following the
observed Memorial Day holiday. Items will be allowed on graves the Thursday
before until Sunday on Easter, Mother's Day, and Father's Day. From April 1
to October 1, no items may be placed on the graves with the exception of cone
vases, which may be placed with fresh cut flowers. Items may be placed on
grave markers and bases as long as they do not protrude past the marker base.
Items that are located on grave markers or bases will be removed if they
protrude past the marker base. Flowers will be allowed in permanent vases
year round. All flags and other decorations, funeral designs, cut flowers,
and all other items placed on lots or graves will be removed by the parks,
recreation, and forestry technician when the same become unsightly, damaged,
or are not placed in compliance with these sections.



   (b)   Artificial flowers and wreaths shall be removed at the
expiration of time limits. If not, such decorations will be removed by the
parks, recreation, and forestry technician and held for fourteen (14) days.
If not then reclaimed, the decorations may be discarded.



   (c)   No glass containers or items of any type will be permitted in
the cemetery. All glass containers or items located in the cemetery will be
removed.



   (d)   In no case shall the city employees be responsible for
articles which may be left on any lot or grave. In all cases, the right is
given to the city to remove from any lot or grave any article which is
unsightly or otherwise objectionable.



(Code 1982, § 6-236.1; Ord. No. 613, § 6-236.1, 4-6-87; Ord. No. 927,
8-5-02; Ord. No. 1295, 11-19-18)



Secs. 14-189—14-205.  Reserved.



DIVISION 3. INTERMENT



Sec. 14-206.  Burial applications.



   No burial in Rose Hill Cemetery or the Rose Garden Cemetery will be
allowed until a burial application is completed by the designated city
employee with the following information:



   (1)   Name and address of applicant.



   (2)   Applicant's relationship to the deceased.



   (3)   Name, date of birth, and date of death of the person to be
buried.



   (4)   Block, section, lot, and space number of which burial is to be
made.



   (5)   Name of the mortician in charge of the body.



   (6)   Date and time of graveside service.



(Code 1982, § 6-230; Ord. No. 599, § 6-231, 9-15-86; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Sec. 14-210.  Vault covers.



   Vault covers shall not be allowed on graves.



(Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Secs. 14-211—14-230.  Reserved.



Sec. 14-207.  Issuance of burial permit; procedures.



   The designated city employee within the public works department shall
approve the burial application setting forth the grave, lot, and block number
upon which the burial is to be made. After procuring the burial application,
the city will stake and inspect the grave space. Double burials will be
allowed if prior arrangements have been made with the public works office.
Temporary grave markers must be used by all mortuaries. The city will not be
held responsible for any temporary markers. Under normal circumstances, the
city will not be responsible for actual digging of the graves.



(Code 1982, §§ 6-230, 6-232; Ord. No. 599, §§ 6-231, 6-232, 9-15-86; Ord.
No. 700, 4-15-91; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Sec. 14-208.  Casket enclosures.



   No person four (4) years of age and over shall be buried in the
cemetery, unless the casket is enclosed in a concrete or steel container. No
wooden or fiberglass outside containers shall be allowed.



(Code 1982, § 6-233; Ord. No. 599, § 6-233, 9-15-86)



Sec. 14-209.  Inadvertent burial or damage.



   Any person who purchases any cemetery lot shall, by such purchase, be
deemed to have agreed, on behalf of himself and his heirs and assigns, to
hold the city harmless for any damages resulting from an inadvertent burial
on the wrong lot or for any damage to any stone, marker or other improvement
placed on the lot so purchased.



(Code 1982, § 6-234; Ord. No. 599, § 6-234, 9-15-86)



DIVISION 4. PERPETUAL CARE



Sec. 14-231.  Perpetual care fund created.



   The common council shall create and maintain a permanent fund from the
gifts or bequests made by any person by will or otherwise, from all sums
derived from the sale of perpetual care, and from sums that may be from time
to time added thereto by the common council, and shall use the income
therefrom for the improvement and care of the cemetery.



(Code 1982, § 6-234; Ord. No. 599, § 6-221, 9-15-86; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Sec. 14-232.  Investment of fund.



   The perpetual care fund shall be invested with interest in such amounts
as may be determined by the finance officer and upon security as acceptable
according to state law.



(Ord. No. 599, § 6-222, 9-15-86)



Sec. 14-233.  Records and accounts of finance officer.



   The city finance officer shall keep a permanent record of all moneys
received for the perpetual care fund, and the amounts paid in or set aside
for general improvement, and shall keep an accurate account of the interest
received and collected and how expended.



(Code 1982, § 6-236; Ord. No. 599, § 6-223, 9-15-86)



Sec. 14-234.  Audit.



   The books and accounts of the finance officer and the securities on
which the perpetual care fund is loaned shall be audited as required for all
accounts of the city by the South Dakota Legislative Audit.



(Code 1982, § 6-237; Ord. No. 599, § 6-224, 9-15-86; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Sec. 14-235.  Extent of care.



   Perpetual care consists of watering the lot, mowing, trimming, raking,
refilling as necessary, reseeding as needed, and all care necessary to
maintain the property to the best of the ability of the city.



(Code 1982, § 6-230; Ord. No. 599, § 6-230, 9-15-86; Ord. No. 927, 8-5-02)



Secs. 14-236—14-250.  Reserved.



ARTICLE VII. PARKS AND RECREATION AREAS*



   *Cross references—Consuming, blending, possessing, alcoholic
beverages in public places prohibited and the disposal of containers
containing alcoholic beverages restricted, § 4-17; animals running at large
prohibited, § 5-1; subdivisions, Ch. 15A; street and park trees, § 19-71 et
seq.; zoning, App. A.



   State law reference—Municipal parks and recreational facilities, SDCL
Ch. 9-38.



Sec. 14-251.  System established.



   There is hereby established in the city a system of public recreation
and playgrounds, and for such purpose the city may acquire, equip and
maintain land, buildings, or other recreational facilities, and expand its
funds therefor.



(Code 1982, § 6-100)



Sec. 14-252.  Parks designated.



   The city's parks and campground, together with all structures,
buildings, improvements and equipment thereon, are the property of the city
and shall be and constitute the city parks.



(Code 1982, § 6-101)



Sec. 14-253.  Management.



   Until and unless otherwise provided for, the management of the city
parks shall be in the hands of the public works administrator and the
supervision shall rest with the common council.



(Code 1982, § 6-102)



Sec. 14-254.  Closure authorized.



   Upon determination that it would be in the best interests of the city
that the city parks or any part thereof be closed to the public for any
reason, the common council shall, without further notice, have the authority
to close all or any part of any city park to public use.



(Code 1982, § 6-103)



ARTICLE VIII. ART IN PUBLIC PLACES



Sec. 14-301.  Purpose.



   The purpose of this article is to provide a means to fund the
acquisition of artwork by the City of Spearfish, which shall become the
city's collection; to provide a means to select artwork for the collection;
to provide for the display of the collection and to provide for the
maintenance and repair of the artwork in the collection.



(Ord. No. 1015, 8-15-05)



Sec. 14-302.  Definitions.



   For the purpose of this article, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.



   City means the City of Spearfish.



   Committee means the art in public places committee created and codified
in § 14-304 of this article.



   Construction project means the construction, rehabilitation,
renovation, remodeling, equipping or improvement of any building, street,
park, utility line or other improvement, either private or for or by the city
commenced after September 1, 2005,  including all associated landscaping,
parking and the like, but excluding any improvements excepted by the city
council after a public hearing thereon.



   Commercial development means a discrete construction project other than
an individual residential unit, a residential development, or a public
facility.



   Individual residential unit means a discrete construction project
resulting in not more than one (1) single family dwelling.



   Public facility means a discrete construction project designed for use
by the general public.



   Residential development means a discrete construction project other
than an individual residential unit designed to be used primarily for human
habitation, including two (2) or more single family dwellings being built
concurrently in the same tract by the same owner or contractor.



   Artwork



      (1)   Includes, but is not limited to, a sculpture, monument,
mural, fresco, relief, painting, fountain, banner, mosaic, ceramic,
weaving,  carving and stained glass. Artwork would normally not include 
landscaping, paving, architectural ornamentation or signs; and



      (2)   Has been, or is intended to be, displayed for more than
two (2) weeks (i) in an open city-owned facility or property, (ii) on the
exterior of any city-owned facility, (iii) inside any city-owed facility in
areas designated as public areas, (iv) on any non-city property if the work
is owned by the city, installed in whole or in part with city funds, or (v)
on any non-city property if the owner has applied for its placement on
private property pursuant to § 14-311 and § 14-312 of this article.



(Ord. No. 1015, 8-15-05)



Sec. 14-303.  Applicability of article.



   All entities purchasing building permits from the City of Spearfish
shall be subject to the provisions of this article.



(Ord. No. 1015, 8-15-05)



Sec. 14-304.  Establishment of the Art in Public Places Committee.



   There is established an art in public places committee. It shall
consist of seven members appointed by the city council who shall serve
without compensation. The members shall serve for periods of three (3) years
each, except that the initial terms of two (2) of such members shall expire
on December 31, 2007, the initial terms of two such members shall expire on
December 31, 2008, and the initial terms of three (3) such members shall
expire on December 31, 2009. All members shall be eligible for reappointment.
The members shall be citizens who are actively interested in the visual arts
and civic improvement.  The function of such committee shall be to perform
the duties set forth in this article.



(Ord. No. 1015, 8-15-05)



Sec. 14-305.  Establishment of the Art in Public Places Fund.



   There is established a fund known as the "art in public places fund"
which shall be credited with funds obtained as art in public places
allocations, secured through grants, as donations, or as otherwise obtained
or determined by the city council.  This fund shall be maintained by the
city finance officer and shall be used for the acquisition, installation,
improvement, and maintenance of artwork to be displayed in the city, the
administration of the art in public places program, and for community public
art education programs not to exceed five percent (5%) of the annual budget.



(Ord. No. 1015, 8-15-05)



Sec.  14-306.  Requirements of entities subject to this article.



   (a)   Before the city issues a valid building permit pursuant to §
6-29 to any entity subject to this article, the entity shall fulfill one of
the following:



      (1)   An application for placement of artwork on private
property has been submitted to the committee and approved by the city council
pursuant to § 14-311 and § 14-312 of this article; or



      (2)   An application for acceptance of artwork to be donated
to the city has been submitted to the committee and approved by the city
council pursuant to § 14-313 and § 14-314 of this article; or



      (3)   The art in public places allocation has been paid.



   (b)   If an entity does not fulfill subpart (1) of this section
prior to the completion of the construction project, the city may assess the
art in public places allocation pursuant to § 14-307 of this article and
this assessment therefore shall become a lien against the real property.



(Ord. No. 1015, 8-15-05)



Sec. 14-307.  Art in Public Places Allocation.



   The art in public places allocation shall be 5% of the building permit
cost which is set aside for the city's art in public places program pursuant
to § 14-306(1)(c) of this article and shall be as follows:



   (1)   The total building valuation upon which the permit cost is set
shall be computed using the latest building valuation data as set forth by
the International Building Code unless, in the opinion of the building
official, a different valuation should be used.



   (2)   If any project is partially funded from any source which
precludes art as an object of expenditure of funds, then this section shall
apply only to the amount of funds not so restricted.



(Ord. No. 1015, 8-15-05)



Sec. 14-308.  Administration.



   The committee shall administer the provisions of this article relating
to acquisition and display of artwork. The committee shall submit to the city
council, not later than March of each year, a report of its activities for
the prior year.  The committee shall also prepare and submit to the city
council, no later than March of each year, an annual plan for the art in
public places program. 



(Ord. No. 1015, 8-15-05)



Sec. 14-309.  Guidelines.



   The committee shall adopt guidelines:



   (1)    To identify suitable artwork for city buildings;



   (2)   To facilitate the preservation of artwork;



   (3)    To prescribe a method or methods for competitive selection of
artwork for display;



   (4)   To prescribe procedures for the selection, acquisition and
display of artwork;



   (5)   To prescribe procedures for the maintenance  of artwork; and



   (6)    To set forth any other matter appropriate to the
administration of this article.



(Ord. No. 1015, 8-15-05)



Sec. 14-310.  Selection and display standards.



   In performing its duties with respect to artwork, the committee shall
give special attention to the following matters:



   (1)   Conceptual compatibility of the design with the immediate
environment of the site;



   (2)   Appropriateness of the design to the function of the site;



   (3)   Compatibility of the design and location with a unified design
character or historical character of the site;



   (4)   Creation of an internal sense of order and desirable
environment for the general community by the design and location of the
artwork;



   (5)   Accessibility to the viewing and appreciation by the public;



   (6)   Preservation and integration of natural features for the
project;



   (7)   Appropriateness of the materials, textures, colors and design
to the expression of the design concept; and



   (8)   Representation of a broad variety of tastes within the
community and the provision of a balanced inventory of artwork to insure a
variety of style, design and media throughout the community.



(Ord. No. 1015, 8-15-05)



Sec. 14-311.  Application procedure for placement of artwork on private
property.



   An application for placement of artwork on private property shall be
submitted to the committee and shall include:



   (1)   Preliminary sketches, photographs, or other documentation of
sufficient nature to indicate the nature of the proposed artwork;



   (2)   An appraisal or other evidence of value of the proposed
artwork, including acquisition and installation costs;



   (3)   Preliminary plans containing such detailed information as may
be required by the committee to adequately evaluate the location of the
artwork in relation to the proposed development, and its compatibility with
the proposed development, including compatibility with the character of
adjacent conforming development parcels and existing neighborhood if
necessary to evaluate the proposal; and



   (4)   A narrative statement to be submitted to the committee to
demonstrate that the artwork will be displayed in an area open and freely
available to the general public, or otherwise provide public accessibility in
an equivalent manner based on the characteristics of the artwork or its
placement on the site.



(Ord. No. 1015, 8-15-05)



Sec. 14-312.  Review of application for placement of artwork on private
property.



   Completed applications shall be submitted to the committee for review
and approval of the artwork.  The committee's recommendation as to the
approval or disapproval of the application shall be forwarded to the city
council which shall have the sole authority to accept or reject or
conditionally accept the application.  Unapproved applications may be
resubmitted to the committee.



(Ord. No. 1015, 8-15-05)



Sec. 14-313.  Application procedure for acceptance of artwork donated to the
city.



   An application for acceptance of artwork to be donated to the city
shall be submitted to the committee and shall include:



   (1)   Preliminary sketches, photographs, models or other
documentation of sufficient descriptive clarity to indicate the nature of the
proposed artwork;



   (2)   An appraisal or other evidence of the value of the proposed
artwork, including acquisition and installation costs.



   (3)   Other information as may be required by the committee to
adequately evaluate the proposed donation of artwork.



(Ord. No. 1015, 8-15-05) 



Sec. 14-314.  Review of application for acceptance of artwork donated to the
city.



   Completed applications shall be submitted to the committee for review
and approval of the donation.  The committee's recommendation as to the
approval or disapproval of the donation shall be forwarded to the city
council which shall have the sole authority to accept or reject or
conditionally accept the donation.  Unapproved applications may be
resubmitted to the committee.



(Ord. No. 1015, passed 8-15-05)



Sec. 14-315.  Artwork purchased with public funds.



   The committee may recommend to the city council the purchase of artwork
with funds from the "art in public places fund," with city funds, or with
grants procured by the city.  A recommendation shall include the type of
artwork considered, an analysis of the constraints applicable to placement of
the artwork, and the costs of acquisition and installation of the artwork.



Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-05)



Sec. 14-316.  Installation of artwork financed with city funds of private
property.



   The committee may install artwork financed or installed either wholly
or in part with funds from the "art in public places fund," with city funds,
or with grants procured by the city, on privately owned property, but only
pursuant to a written agreement between the committee, acting on behalf of
the city, and the owner specifying the proprietary interests in the artwork
and specifying other provisions deemed necessary or desirable by the city
attorney. In addition, such written agreement shall specify that the private
property owner shall assure:



   (1)   That the installation of the artwork will be done in a manner
which will protect the artwork and the public;



   (2)    That the artwork will be maintained in good condition; and



   (3)   That insurance and indemnification will be provided as is
appropriate.



(Ord. No. 1015, 8-15-05)



Sec. 14-317.  Display of art in public places.



   (a)   Artwork selected and implemented pursuant to the provisions of
this article may be placed in, on or about any public place or, by agreement
with the owner thereof, any private property with substantial public exposure
in and around the city.  Artwork owned by the city may also be loaned for
exhibition elsewhere, upon such terms and conditions as deemed necessary by
the committee.



   (b)   City officials responsible for the design and construction of
public improvements in the city shall make appropriate space available for
the placement of artwork, in consultation with the committee. The committee
shall advise the department responsible for the particular public improvement
of the committee's decision regarding the design, execution and placement of
artwork in connection with such project. For any proposed artwork requiring
an extraordinary operation or maintenance expense, the committee shall obtain
prior written approval of the department head responsible for such operation
or maintenance before approving the same.



   (c)    Whenever feasible, installation, maintenance, alteration,
refinishing and moving of artwork shall be done in consultation with the
artist.



   (d)    The committee shall maintain a detailed record of all
artwork, including site drawings, photographs, designs, names of artists and
names of architects whenever feasible.  The committee shall attempt to give
appropriate recognition to the artists and publicity and promotion regarding
artwork.



(Ord. No. 1015, 8-15-05)



Sec. 14-318.  Ownership and maintenance of artwork.



   (a)   All artwork acquired with funds from the "art in public places
fund," with city funds, or with grants procured by the city, or by donation
pursuant to this article pursuant to § 14-313 and § 14-314 shall be
acquired in the name of, and title shall be held by, the city.



   (b)   All artwork placed on the private property pursuant to §
14-311 and § 14-312 shall remain the property of the applicant; the
obligation to provide all maintenance necessary to preserve the artwork in
good condition shall remain with the owner of the site. 



      (1)   Maintenance of artwork shall include without limitation:
preservation of the artwork in good condition to the satisfaction of the
committee, protection of the artwork against physical defacement, mutilation
or alteration, and securing and maintaining insurance to be determined by the
City of Spearfish. 



      (2)   In addition to all other remedies provided by law, in
the event the owner fails to maintain the artwork, upon reasonable notice,
the city may perform all necessary repairs, maintenance, or secure insurance,
and the costs therefor shall become a lien against the real property.



(Ord. No. 1015, 8-15-05)



Sec. 14-319.  Removal or alteration of artwork.



   Artwork installed on or integrated into a construction project pursuant
to the provisions of this chapter shall not be removed or altered without the
approval of the city council.  If such artwork is knowingly removed or
altered without prior approval, the City of Spearfish may pursue any
available civil or criminal remedies or penalties.



(Ord. No. 1015, passed 8-15-05)



Sec. 14-320.  Exemptions.



   The following are exempt from the provisions of this chapter:



   (1)    All artwork in the collections of, or on display at, or under
the auspices of, the High Plains Heritage Center, Spearfish Public Library,
or Black Hills State University; and



   (2)    All artwork in display in private city offices or other areas
of city-owned facilities which are not generally frequented by the public.



(Ord. No. 1015, 8-15-05)
